King Edward VII of England to be Crowned Next May 46

Proclamation Read on St. James's Balcony

Guards in Shining Armor, Solemn Ceremony

The proclamation that King Edward VII of England will be crowned on May 12, 1937 was read today on the balcony of St. James's Palace according to ancient custom. The royal coat of arms hung high on the bell tower, where the King resided. Officials gathered on the platform, including military officers in shining armor, those who wore the armor of Edward VI (1547-1557). The King's Hand Grenade Guards were lined up in the garden below the platform, mixed with the military band of the Coldstream Guards. With three military bugle calls, the Grand Master of Ceremonies Sir Horatio Halliston read the proclamation. The text of the proclamation was about a yard wide. The knight finished reading it in seven minutes, shouting "God Save the King." The audience did not respond with cheers, apparently because they were awed by the solemnity of the ceremony. When the knight read the proclamation, a gramophone and a loudspeaker were placed in front of him so that the audience could hear it. After the ceremony, the officials marched in formation to the Royal Exchange, where the proclamation was read again. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

George Bernard Shaw's Humorous Business Card 47

Disabled Children Are Not Suitable to Live in the Current World

Why Not Throw Them Into the Fire to Make Them Ascend to the Kingdom of Heaven

London: Today, when a charity auction was held to raise money for disabled children, there was a business card written by playwright George Bernard Shaw, which stated that the current world is not suitable for children to live in. Why not let these disabled children have fun for one day, and then, while they are sleeping, throw them into the fire and make them ascend to the Kingdom of Heaven? This business card was then purchased by a person for 10 pounds and was ordered to be burned on the spot. (National News dispatch on the 28th)

Page 8

American Industrial Consumption of Tung Oil Increases Sharply 48

Most of it Comes from China

(Washington) According to a report released today by the Chemical Testing Department of the Ministry of Commerce, American industrial consumption of tung oil has increased by 70% since 1931. The total consumption in 1935 was 127,600,000 pounds. This tung oil comes almost entirely from China, with only a small amount supplied by the Gulf Coast of the United States, where a tung oil industry is gradually emerging. Taking the average price of 18 cents per pound this year as the standard for calculation, the tung oil used by the American paint industry in 1936 accounts for about 75% of the total amount. The total consumption in 1935 was 98,440,000 pounds. The oilcloth industry ranked second, with consumption in 1935 of 10,391,000 pounds, a significant increase compared to 7,300,000 pounds in 1932. The tung oil used by the pigment industry last year totaled 2,003,000 pounds, compared to 713,000 pounds in 1932. In 1935, the consumption of other industries totaled 10,756,000 pounds, compared to 7,892,000 pounds in 1932. The amount of tung oil used by the electrical industry, the wood board industry, waterproofing compounds, car oilcloth, and raincoat manufacturing is also considerable. (National News dispatch on the 28th)

League of Nations Discussion on Opium Suppression Concludes; Requests Japan to Punish Drug Traffickers; Chinese Representative Expresses Gratitude for International Cooperation 49

(Geneva) During the League of Nations Opium Committee's discussion on the current situation of narcotics in China, both the American representative, Fowler, and the Chinese representative, Hu Shih-tse, criticized Japan for failing to take adequate measures to prohibit Japanese and Korean individuals from trafficking drugs. This discussion concluded last night. Before the adjournment of the committee, Hu Shih-tse expressed his gratitude to the governments of all countries for jointly urging Japan to suppress drug traffickers, and stated that the Chinese government would do everything in its power to eliminate this scourge. He then mentioned Fowler's candid remarks, hoping that if the U.S. government obtained information similar to that revealed by its representative, it would immediately notify the Chinese government. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

(Geneva) The Advisory Committee on Opium Problems of the League of Nations continued its meeting today. The American representative, Fowler (Assistant Director of the Far Eastern Division of the State Department), delivered a speech, once again strongly condemning the activities of Japanese individuals trafficking drugs within Chinese territory. He stated that in the Hongkou area of Shanghai alone, there were no fewer than thirty to forty opium dens, and that the Japanese authorities were fully aware of this but had never taken measures to prohibit them. It is generally believed that the Opium Committee will once again petition the Japanese government to take effective measures to punish its citizens trafficking drugs in North China. It is reported that the British and American governments have already notified the Japanese government of this matter, urging them to pay attention to it. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

(Geneva) The Advisory Committee on Opium Problems of the League of Nations continued its meeting today. First, the Portuguese representative, Vasconcelos, spoke, strongly requesting the Japanese representative to once again ask his government to take effective measures to curb the drug trafficking activities of its citizens. He stated that the Japanese representative had, nine years prior, already declared in the name of his government that they were willing to take effective action. The Chinese representative, Hu Shih-tse, then spoke, saying, "It must not be forgotten that a portion of Chinese territory is not managed by our own government officials. However, our government has taken all necessary measures within its scope of duty for opium suppression work. If the Japanese government could restrain its citizens from engaging in drug trafficking, it would be a great benefit to opium suppression work, and the two nations, China and Japan, would also understand each other better." Thereupon, the Japanese representative, Ito, stood up and replied, stating that his government had not been lenient towards drug traffickers. If the measures previously taken proved ineffective, then other measures would be adopted upon verification. He also stated that his government genuinely intended to eradicate illegal trade. At this point, the American representative, Fowler, questioned him and once again criticized the Japanese for trafficking drugs in Shanghai. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

Minister of Public Works Transferred to Colonial Secretary 50

Belongs to the National Labour Party

Familiar with the Situation in Palestine

(London) The order to transfer Ormsby-Gore, the Minister of Public Works, to the position of Colonial Secretary has been officially announced. However, the selection of a successor for the Minister of Public Works has not yet been determined. It is likely that Lord Trawell, the Under-Secretary of Education, will be promoted. Because Trawell belongs to the National Labour Party, and the current cabinet is advocating "national unity," with the departure of one National Labour Party cabinet member (Thomas), it is fitting that another National Labour Party cabinet member be appointed, so that the balance of power among the political parties can be maintained. It is reported that the newly appointed Colonial Secretary, Ormsby-Gore, previously served as an administrative officer in Palestine in 1918, and is extremely familiar with the special circumstances there. In 1922, he was transferred to become the Under-Secretary of the Colonial Office. When the Labour Party cabinet was formed in 1924, he resigned due to differing party affiliations. In 1929, when former Prime Minister MacDonald formed the National Cabinet, Gore made a comeback and resumed his original position. In 1931, he was promoted to Postmaster General, and in the same year, he was transferred to Minister of Public Works. In 1932, he represented Britain at the League of Nations Mandates Commission. Now that the Palestine issue has suddenly become tense, it is necessary to have a high-ranking official familiar with the local situation to cope with the difficulties and immediately resolve the disputes. The reason why Gore was able to quickly succeed Thomas as Colonial Secretary is likely due to this. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Disturbances Continue Unabated Throughout Palestine 51

British Garrison Increased to Six Regiments and One Battalion

Jerusalem Today, Arabs staged riots throughout Palestine. Bombing incidents occurred in Haifa, Jaffa, Safed, and other places. In Kfar Shmaryahu, two Arabs died and one was injured. In the city of Tyre, three Arabs were also injured in clashes with the police. Road guards in Safed repeatedly opened fire, dispersing Arabs who were plotting to destroy railway tracks. Orange groves along the Jewish settlement in the Akko region were burned down. The police station in Nazareth was shot at by Arabs, but there were no casualties. In the Old City of Jerusalem, a British policeman was shot in a vital area near an Austrian hospital by Arab rioters. At the same time, a British artillery unit has set out from Egypt and is expected to impose martial law at any time. A group of soldiers from the Bedfordshire and Hertfordshire brigades also departed from Alexandria, Egypt, last night. The British military strength here will be increased to six infantry regiments and one armored car battalion. Last night, an Associated Press reporter, under police protection, visited a Jewish prayer site. Traditionally, people pray there day and night, but last night, despite it being a Jewish holiday, there were only three elderly men. (National Telegram, 28th)

Jerusalem The state of unrest throughout Palestine is still serious. The families of British officials here have already left the country for refuge. Admiral Pound, Commander-in-Chief of the British Mediterranean Fleet, arrived at the port of Haifa yesterday aboard the flagship "Barham" and immediately transferred to a plane to fly to Jerusalem to confer with British High Commissioner Wauchope on the current situation. The Jewish Agency recently issued a declaration discussing the issue of Jewish immigration. Abu al-Ghadhi, secretary of the Arab Higher Committee, also issued a declaration in response, stating, "The land in Palestine is small and cannot accommodate the immigration of the Jewish people. The Jewish people's idea of taking Palestine as a place to live and thrive hinders the Arab autonomy movement." It is rumored that the Arab Higher Committee intends to hold a meeting with the executive of the Jewish Agency to discuss ways to resolve the disputes. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Jerusalem Today's official announcement states that the authorities now have tear gas available for use when necessary. The Special Commissioner in Palestine, Wauchope, does not want to implement a plan that could cause death or injury, so he intends to use tear gas to maintain order when necessary. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

Italy Makes Radio Propaganda; British Government Raises Questions 52

(London) Colonial Secretary Malcolm MacDonald stated in the House of Commons today regarding the situation in Palestine that the Arab National Congress issued a resolution on May 7, calling on Arabs to engage in passive resistance. The Arab Strike Committee and Muslim leaders in Jerusalem, as well as the so-called Jaffa National Defense League and a prominent Arab reporter, have all issued declarations containing somewhat inflammatory language. The British government is very satisfied with the measures taken by the Special Commissioner in Palestine to deal with the unrest and is confident that he will be able to control the overall situation. MacDonald also acknowledged that Italy is making radio propaganda to Arabs, stating that Foreign Secretary Eden has raised questions with the Italian government about this. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

French Labor Unrest Expands, Threatening Socialist Government 55

Labor-Management Negotiations Break Down

(Paris) Although the striking workers in the metalworking factories around the capital have been staying in the factories for the past two days, they have not caused disturbances or prevented the managers of the factories from entering. Labor leaders have now issued a statement saying that this labor unrest is purely occupational in nature and has no political implications. In the past, whenever there was labor unrest, the factories often hired unemployed workers to replace the striking workers, thereby undermining the strike movement. The workers in the metalworking factories decided to stay in the factories to prevent such situations from occurring. As for the demands made by these workers, such as the implementation of a 40-hour work week and the signing of labor contracts by union representatives on behalf of the workers with the employers, these cannot be regarded as excessive. In addition, it is generally believed that these workers have been making these demands for more than a day. Recently, because of the electoral victory of the parties belonging to the left-wing Popular Front, their momentum has been strengthened, and they have begun to strike in the hope of implementing their original demands. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

(Paris) The trend of strikes in which workers stay in the factories but do not work is now rapidly spreading to machine factories throughout France. Large factories in the country, such as the largest automobile factory in France, with 32,000 workers, are now also participating in the strike movement. French Prime Minister Sarraut is paying close attention to this matter and has repeatedly held meetings in the Ministry of Interior and the Executive Yuan. Many members of parliament believe that this labor unrest is a move by the Communist Party to make things difficult for the new Socialist government. However, the Socialist Party denies that this movement has revolutionary implications, saying that the workers' actions are merely intended to avoid being locked out by the factory when their demands for wage increases and improved treatment have not been resolved. This labor unrest uses a new tactic: staying in the factory but not working, so that the factory will not be able to recruit new workers to undermine the labor movement. It is generally recognized that this is one of the most effective tactics in recent labor unrest. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

(Paris) The Ministry of Labor has drafted a solution to the metalworking industry strike, namely that the employers and worker representatives should study the various demands raised by the striking workers, and that the employers should not punish the strikers after they return to work. It is reported that the employers have accepted the above solution, but on the condition that the workers return to work first. The union representatives also believe that this method is sufficient to resolve the disputes between labor and management and have accepted it. Labor Minister Frossard has also scheduled to invite representatives from both labor and management at 4:00 PM tomorrow to begin negotiations, so that the method of signing labor contracts with the employers by the workers belonging to the union representatives can be implemented. Frossard has announced to the press that all metalworking factories will be able to resume work uniformly, and that tomorrow afternoon's negotiations will proceed smoothly. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

(Paris) After the labor unrest occurred in the metalworking factories in the suburbs, the striking workers stayed in the factory buildings overnight, but the police have not intervened, except to maintain order in the vicinity. In addition, labor and management have agreed on the basis for resolving the dispute yesterday, that the union should come forward to represent the workers belonging to it and sign labor contracts with the employers. It was also decided that Labor Minister Frossard would invite representatives from both sides at 4:00 PM today to conduct negotiations based on the above basis. This method was the result of day-long consultations yesterday between representatives of labor and management from various factories, as well as Prime Minister Sarraut, Labor Minister Frossard, and labor union leaders. After this consultation, the employers finally agreed that the union could come forward to represent the workers belonging to it and sign labor contracts, but on the condition that all striking workers immediately return to work and no longer stay in the factory buildings. The employers also promised that they would not punish the striking workers after they returned to work. With the opinions of both sides becoming more harmonious, the agreed method will be submitted to the delegation of striking workers this morning. If there are no objections, then negotiations between labor and management can be held as scheduled this afternoon to seek a final resolution. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

Japan's Trade is Subjected to Oppression; the Key Lies Entirely in Great Britain 56

Business Circles Send Representatives to Seek Reconciliation

Intend to Implement a Trade Protection Act Against Australia

(Tokyo) Japanese trade is currently subjected to comprehensive oppression. The leadership of the Economic Federation is now proceeding with the selection of representatives to go to Great Britain.

The government is determined to implement retaliatory measures against Australia and has decided to launch a Trade Protection Act and simultaneously implement an import licensing system to prohibit the raising of prices for滞貨 [stagnant] wool.

The Japan Economic Federation convened a Trade Promotion Committee on the 28th, requesting four people to attend, including wool industry representatives Tsurumi and Tsukawaki, and flour industry representatives Shoda and Nakamura, to solicit opinions on countermeasures against the Japan-Australia problem. However, because a conclusion was not reached, it was decided to continue the meeting on the 29th. In addition to Tsurumi, Shoda, and Tsukawaki still attending, representatives from the cotton industry, the rayon industry, and the trade industry were invited to decide on countermeasures to be implemented against Australia in order to advise the government. Spanish Fascist Leader Makes a Scene in Court 60

Madrid Rivera, the son of the former Spanish dictator General Primo de Rivera and leader of the current Spanish Fascist Party, was sentenced to five months in prison for possessing military arms. When the sentence was pronounced, Rivera shouted "Spain Arise!" and his family members echoed him. Court order was disrupted. The court president ordered the court to adjourn immediately. Rivera jumped onto the president's seat, verbally abused the judges, snatched a lawyer's top hat, threw it at the president's head, then tore off his prison clothes, destroyed them, stepped on them, and shouted for Spain to rise up and resist the corrupt judges. The Fascist leader stomped the president's seat, kicked over the judges' seats, swept all the documents on the counters to the ground, and destroyed the stone statue in the court. Police then arrested several people involved in the disturbance and order was restored. (National Telegram, 29th)

British Ship "Queen Mary" Advances Across the Atlantic; Speed Exceeds the "Normandie" 61

(London) According to a Reuters special correspondent on board the "Queen Mary", the "Queen Mary" is sailing faster and is expected to increase its speed significantly tomorrow. The weather is fine and the ocean is calm. The ship must arrive at Ambrose Lighthouse on Sunday morning to win the Atlantic speed title. The title was won by the French mail ship "Normandie" in June last year during its maiden voyage, taking four days, three hours, and five minutes to travel from Southampton to New York, with an average speed of 29.98 nautical miles. Yesterday, the average speed of the Queen Mary was 28.38 nautical miles. (Reuter's dispatch, 29th)

Qiantang River Bridge; Caisson Anchor Destroyed by Water 78

(Hangzhou) The caisson project for the No. 4 pier of the Qiantang River Railway Bridge is currently underway, pouring concrete. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the river suddenly rose, and wooden rafts from upstream flowed downstream, and all the caisson anchors were washed away by the impact. They flowed with the waves to the foot of the Liuhe Pagoda Mountain. The caisson weighs 720 tons and the cost of labor and materials is more than 15,000 yuan. It must wait for the tide to rise before it can be towed back to its original location and installed. The caisson project is scheduled to be completed within this year, and the entire project will be completed by the end of June next year. (Special dispatch, 29th)

The works may also be confiscated. However, this does not apply if the translation acquired copyright before the original work was registered. Negotiations on the Xiamen Japanese Residents' Perpetual Lease Rights Case 102

Japanese Consul's Visit to the Province Yields Principles

Japanese Monk Forcibly Excavates and Moves Civilian Graves

Xiamen Correspondence: Recently, the Xiamen Municipal Government has delayed approving the case of Japanese monk Shinhuiyun, who accepted a donation of land from Japanese residents Zhang Youji and Lei Yiming from Taiwan at the former site of Daguanyuan to apply to the Municipal Government for permission to construct a Dong Sect temple, "Hongan-ji." The Municipal Government believes that in law, our country does not recognize the perpetual lease rights of foreigners' real estate. The Japanese Consul has subsequently raised the entire issue of the perpetual lease rights of Japanese residents in Xiamen, seeking to further obtain legal recognition. However, this has also been unsuccessful. Japanese Consul Yamada Yoshitaro flew to the province on the 21st to meet with Chen Yi and directly negotiated this case.

After several negotiations, the Japanese Consul returned to Xiamen on the 25th and visited Mayor Li Shilin again on the 26th to discuss the matter. According to provincial news, the Provincial Government has reached an agreement with Japanese Consul Yamada on the issue of Japanese residents purchasing and leasing land in Xiamen, with the fundamental principle of not infringing on sovereignty and not exceeding the treaty. Other minor issues will be handled by the Xiamen Municipal Government, which will deliberate the situation and continue negotiations with Yamada based on this principle. Li made arrangements to visit Chen Yi in the province again on the 28th after consulting with the Japanese Consul. In addition, a week ago, the Xiamen Tax Bureau, upon order from the Provincial Government, imposed a deed tax of 4% of the rental price on the perpetual lease land and houses of foreign nationals in Xiamen, plus an additional 10% for education fees. Furthermore, within the area requested by the Japanese monk at Daguanyuan, there are over 80 civilian graves. After the Japanese Consul urged the matter, the Municipal Government issued a notice in mid-April, stating, "Construction will commence within the area, and all graves must be relocated within one month to receive compensation from the Public Works Bureau." Subsequently, some grave owners within the area submitted deeds after relocation, requesting payment of compensation. The Municipal Government instructed the Public Works Bureau to respond, "This Bureau's notice for relocation is to prevent encroachment and profiteering. Since the residents have purchased the land at a price and have a contract to rely on, the determination of ownership is already clear. It should be known that this Bureau only has the responsibility to protect the legally acquired rights of the people and has no right to freely dispose of them. External rumors should not be lightly believed." Later, those who submitted deeds requesting preservation also received the same response. At the same time, the Public Works Bureau also stopped issuing relocation fees. As a result, everyone believed that the Daguanyuan land negotiation had made headway, and the construction of the temple could be canceled. Therefore, they waited and watched and did not relocate their graves any further. However, on May 24th and 25th, the Japanese monk's side suddenly and unilaterally hired workers

to continuously excavate and relocate 25 graves. When asked, they said, "All graves will be completely cleared to begin construction." On the 26th, five representatives of the grave owners, including Zhuang Dachuan, Guo Jinbang, and Su Zhusan, went to the Public Works Bureau to petition for a halt. The Bureau agreed to report to the Municipal Government to negotiate with the Japanese Consul, temporarily suspending excavation and awaiting a thorough investigation. If it is indeed proven to be the property rights of Japanese residents, the Bureau will instruct Chinese citizens to relocate voluntarily, without the need for Japanese monks to relocate on their behalf.

The Provincial Government recently promulgated the Provisional Regulations on the Rental of Land and Houses by Foreign Churches, ordering all counties and cities to comply. This was also prompted by the Hongan-ji case. The original text is as follows: "Article 1: Foreign churches may rent land and construct or purchase houses in the interior in the name of the church to establish churches, hospitals, or schools that are permitted by treaties between their country and China. Article 2: Foreign churches shall comply with current and future laws and taxes of China when renting land to construct or purchase houses in the interior. Article 3: Foreign churches shall jointly submit applications with the owners to the governing office for approval when renting land to construct or purchase houses in the interior. The contract shall only then be valid. Article 4: The governing office shall not approve applications for foreign churches to rent land in the interior to construct or purchase houses if the area exceeds what is necessary. Article 5: If it is found that foreign churches are using rented land to construct or purchase houses in the interior for profit-making or business purposes, the governing office may prohibit it or revoke the rental or purchase. Article 6: Before the implementation of these provisional regulations, foreign churches should retroactively submit reports to the governing office for land and houses already occupied in the interior. If the land is purchased outright, it will be considered a perpetual lease. Article 7: These provisional regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (May 28th)

Japan's Northeast Immigration Plan 103

Failed Radical Policies, Adopted Gradual Strategies

Planned Immigration of One Million Households Over Twenty Years

Japanese People Extol the Fertile Land of Eastern Manchuria

Changchun Correspondence: Japan's immigration to the Northeast used to be very aggressive, but it has repeatedly failed. Now it is changing its plan and is studying concrete methods for current implementation, generally adopting a gradual strategy and considering financial conditions, etc. In the first year, 20,000 people will be immigrated to various parts of northern Manchuria. The area of each household's arable land is planned to be 2 chōbu of paddy field and 8 chōbu of dry land, totaling approximately 10 chōbu. Matters such as publicity and recruitment for immigration will be managed by the Manchuria Immigration Association established by Japanese residents in Changchun. As for land purchase, cultivation guidance, and finance, these will be managed by the newly established Manchuria Colonization Association by the Japanese. The issue of how much the subsidy amount will be is quite noteworthy. The previous experimental immigration was generally around 2,000 yuan. This time, it seems to be a number of 2,500 yuan to 3,000 yuan. Even if it is 2,000 yuan per household, a million-household immigration plan, even if it is said to be a twenty-year continuing project, will require several hundred million yuan in funding. Whether this funding can be afforded by Japan's current financial situation will determine the success or failure of the immigration issue. Recently, the relevant authorities in Japan have begun to discuss this issue, and considering Finance Minister Baba's repeated statements on the active policy towards "Manchukuo," as well as the national defense perspective held by the central departments of the Japanese Army, there is an absolute need for immigration to "Manchukuo."

According to Suzuki, a Japanese inspector of the Railway Administration, who inspected eastern Manchuria, the area along the Ninglin and Linmi Railways is an area for Japanese and Korean immigrants. The land is exceptionally fertile, the water conservancy is convenient, and the surrounding scenery is no different from Japan. It is located south of Harbin, and there are two coal mines, Jixi and Didao, along the railway line. As long as people live there, economic development will be possible.

Tangshan Kailuan Coal Mine Strike 104

Workers Demand Continuous Shifts and Resort to Passive Resistance

The Strike Has Not Subsided, and the Mine Area is Under Strict Guard

Tianjin Correspondence: The Tangshan Kailuan Coal Mine experienced a strike on the 23rd of this month. Although the Tianjin Mining Bureau has stated to the outside world that the strike is not serious and will subside quickly, according to news from Tangshan, the situation is still serious. The city of Tangshan is effectively under a kind of undeclared martial law, guarding against any kind of riot. The cause of this strike is that some underground and external workers felt that their lives were becoming increasingly difficult and that their income was insufficient to maintain them. They demanded that the mine allow continuous shifts to increase their income. Since this spring, they have raised this matter with the labor-management liaison office stationed at the mine, but it has not been approved. The mine refused the request for the reason that the sales of coal from Kailuan have not been strong in recent years, and there is too much stock. Last autumn, a five-day work week was implemented to reduce stockpiles and save expenses. Workers conscientiously implement the eight-hour system, so everyone has work to do and does not have to stop work for one day each week, reducing workers and suffering unemployment. At the same time, they also vigorously suppressed the behavior of [workers] taking over the work of others, bullying the weak, and being violent against the minority. Regarding the mine's surface workers, most belong to contractor gangs. The work is usually measured and not timed. For example, worker A digs one ton of coal per day and receives two jiao; digging two tons yields four jiao; and more is added accordingly. In the past, strong workers bullied the weak. Worker A was supposed to work two shifts a day, but they ended up working three or four shifts, and also took away the work of worker B. Although worker B had the name of a worker, they could only work at most six or seven shifts in a month. Since last autumn, due to efforts to rectify the situation, these malpractices have been almost completely eradicated. On average, each worker can work twenty-five or six shifts per month, earning about twenty yuan or seventeen or eight yuan in wages. The mine has indeed achieved the goal of not laying off workers to maintain the livelihood of the majority. However, the general workers who usually rely on bullying the weak and seizing work are very dissatisfied. They repeatedly launched passive resistance movements, demanding that the mine restore the old system and needing continuous shifts. The mine ignored them. Its response to the workers was nothing more than two points: Allowing continuous shifts would increase coal production, leading to more stockpiles and greater losses for the mine. The current business situation is not good, and there is no need to increase production. If production is restricted due to allowing the far shift, it will be necessary to lay off some workers. The mine cannot bear to benefit a few people while disregarding the interests of the majority. The world labor system advocates the "three eights." Now workers work eight hours a day, which is in line with this. Allowing continuous shifts means that each person works twelve to sixteen hours. Over time, their energy will not be able to keep up, which will directly harm the workers' own health and indirectly affect the mine's production. Based on these two points, the mine explained to the workers. However, the mine's words fell on deaf ears, and the workers were still unwilling to give up. At 2:00 PM on the 23rd, some off-shift workers, such as Qian Yongze and Cong Dehai, held wooden sticks, hoes, and other tools at the mine entrance to prevent the underground workers from going down the well to change shifts, resulting in a reduction of over 600 tons of coal produced that day. At that time, the mine bureau mobilized a large team of armed mine police to disperse the blindly following workers and arrest nine people, including Qian Yongze, sending them to the court. The off-shift workers, seeing their comrades arrested, gathered to rescue them, clashing with the mine police. Fifteen people were slightly or seriously injured, and two policemen were also injured. The order was greatly disrupted. The mine police temporarily announced martial law, prohibiting workers from entering or exiting, and guarding the mine entrance to prevent sabotage by rioters. However, underground workers Li Shun, Jiao Dianrong, and others held weapons to threaten workers in various trades to stop working and go on strike together. At 4:00 PM, over a thousand workers gathered in the mine, intending to rush out of the mine bureau and march along the streets to the Tangshan Office of the puppet Eastern Hebei Government to petition. The mine police prevented them from listening, and another conflict occurred. Mine policeman Huang Fengqun was severely beaten. The mine police, feeling overwhelmed, fired warning shots, but the workers continued to advance. The puppet Tangshan Public Security Bureau received a report and mobilized a large team of police to assist in the suppression, which finally restored peace. Over thirty rifles of the mine police were confiscated by the Public Security Bureau police to prevent another tragic bloodshed. The 24th was a tense day. Workers gathered several times, planning to surround the court and forcibly demand the release of the workers arrested by the mine police. Fearing incidents, the court ordered the nine workers in custody to be released on bail pending trial. The workers sent out several representatives to the labor-management liaison office stationed at the mine, demanding that the following articles be allowed: Allow continuous shifts. Do not dismiss the leading representatives. There should be no more abuse of workers. The office immediately telegraphed the Tianjin Mining Bureau. The Mining Bureau believed that the workers' demands were unreasonable and advocated a tough stance. On the 25th, it replied by telegram to Wei Zidun, the director of the labor-management liaison office, and Zhang Guanru, the secretary, ordering them to handle the matter severely. Wei and Zhang followed the instructions and issued a notice dismissing all ten of the ringleaders, including Qian Yongze, and forbidding them from ever being re-employed. Because of this, the workers became even more angry. Some expressed sympathy for those who were dismissed and continued to be passive. Wei and Zhang gave four speeches to the workers before and after using loudspeakers, advising them to resume work, but this was ineffective. The mine was full of police, with strict guards and cut off access. On the morning of the 26th, although a few workers went down the well, no coal was seen coming out by the evening. Zhao Lei, the captain of the puppet Tangshan Security Corps, and Lü Liangchen, the director of the Public Security Bureau, specially assisted Wei Zidun in establishing a mediation committee to try to mediate. If the progress is smooth, the strike may not escalate.

Guangdong Construction Department Plans to Establish Silk Factories 105

Shunde Factory Site in Rongqi

Nanhai Factory Site Undecided

Guangzhou Communication: He Qilong, Director of the Construction Department of Guangdong Province, has decided to establish two silk factories to develop the province's silk industry. Some days ago, he sent Huang Yong'an, director of the silk department of the provincial textile factory, to Nanhai and Shunde counties to survey and select sites. After receiving the order, Huang completed the survey and yesterday submitted the investigation report and survey results to the Construction Department. After reviewing the report, the department ordered Liao Chongzhen, Director of the Silk Bureau, and Lin Shiduo and Zhang NieFeng, section chiefs of the department, to jointly review it for approval. The department has now reviewed and approved the results, stating that the report on the Shunde factory site describes in detail the conditions in Chencun, Lecong, Rongqi, and Daliang. The report also lists the advantages and disadvantages of establishing a factory in each location, and it is considered that the Rongqi Beibiansha area in Shunde County is the most suitable. This is because the area has the advantages of convenient transportation, clean water sources, lower construction costs, concentrated raw materials, and easy promotion to inspire other silk factories. As for the Nanhai factory site, compared to Guanshan and Lanshi, Lanshi is more suitable. Guanshan has a low-lying terrain, making it prone to flooding, and has inconvenient transportation and polluted water sources, which are major shortcomings for a silk factory. Lanshi, in addition to the advantages mentioned in the original report, is close to Lecong and Lianglong in Shunde, and Jiujiang in Nanhai, all of which are silk cocoon production areas, ensuring a sufficient supply of raw materials. Moreover, it is adjacent to Shiwan and Pingbu, Xiaochong, Luzhou, Ma'ao, and Xinlong Shuiteng in Shunde, where silk factories are densely located, making it easy to demonstrate improved silk production techniques. Therefore, it is most suitable for establishing a factory. The original report mentioned that the old site of the Yonghe Lun Silk Factory, close to the Lanshi Railway Station, is a pity because the area is too small and using civilian houses could cause disturbances. However, since the old Yonghe Lun site is inconvenient, it seems possible to find another site, which should be easy to handle.

Epidemic Spreads in Disaster Areas of Western Anhui 106

Disaster Victims Eat Anything to Survive

Resulting in Successive Deaths

Wuhu Communication: Hundreds of thousands of disaster-stricken people in Huoqiu, Liu'an, and Hefei counties in Anhui Province have resorted to slaughtering and eating corpses in the market due to the lack of food during this lean season. Although the Central Relief Commission, the Anhui Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, and various parties of the Red Swastika Society have successively sent personnel with funds to provide relief and have opened porridge kitchens in the disaster areas where survival depends on relief, it is ultimately a drop in the bucket. According to a telegram from Liu Xichun, a special commissioner of the Red Swastika Society distributing relief in the disaster area, all parties are deeply concerned about the severity of the disaster and are still trying their best to provide relief. Recently, the Central Relief Commission allocated another 5,000 yuan for relief in Liu'an and 2,000 yuan in Hefei. The Red Swastika Society has allocated 9,000 yuan to Huoqiu County, 1,500 yuan to Liu'an, and 1,000 yuan to Hefei, all of which are being distributed. The Commander-in-Chief of the Suppression of Bandits in the Border Areas of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Provinces, deeply moved by the situation, held a fundraising performance in Liu'an and raised more than 2,700 yuan, which was used to open four porridge kitchens and a shelter for disaster-stricken children. Currently, many refugees in the disaster areas are eating anything to survive, resulting in successive deaths and the widespread spread of epidemics. The tragic situation is unbearable to witness and has become a living hell. Upon receiving the news, the Wuhu Red Swastika Society purchased a large quantity of medicine and sent it to the disaster area for medical relief. (27th)

Suzhou Public Security Bureau Pays Attention to Traitors 111

He issued a notice to the first, second, and third sub-bureaus in the city and the detective team some days ago, ordering subordinate officers and police to pay close attention to the activities of traitors, especially in Fengdou.

Four Major Construction Bureau Projects 112

The Suzhou-Jiaxing Railway will begin selling tickets and opening to traffic next month. The Wuxian Construction Bureau will soon begin work on four major projects that are being prepared for opening: the Xiangmen city gate, Xiangmen Road, Xinhua Bridge, and Xing Lion Bridge. The planned Xiangmen Road will be 1,000 meters long, from the Suzhou-Jiaxing Railway Huang Guagua Bridge Station to the Xiangmen city gate. It is planned to build a solid 8-meter wide coal road. Xinhua Bridge will be a bridge over the moat outside the city, about 100 meters long. In the future, this bridge will be the second longest bridge in the county, second only to the Shi Dai Bridge on the Suzhou-Jiaxing Highway. The Xiangmen city gate will have a vehicle gate, and the Xing Lion Bridge will be more than 10 meters long. The total cost is estimated to be more than 20,000 yuan, and the funds are already available.

Wuxi Actively Handles Land Registration 113

The County Land Administration Bureau, after starting land registration in the third and fourth districts in early March this year, has also established registration sub-offices in Shizhang, Xushe, Nanfangquan, Jiahe, Xuxiang, and Outangqiao. Recently, the registration work has been unusually busy. In order to expand its business, the bureau has specially recruited 100 receptionists to practice rural area registration work. Currently, the land in Shizhang and other six places is expected to be completed around the 20th of next month. Starting on July 1, the land registration of the old Fuan Township in the Fourth District and the Fifth, Sixth, and Seventh Districts will be carried out, with a deadline of the end of August, in order to complete the first phase of land registration.

Dredging Project to Be Completed 114

The dredging of rivers by labor conscription in various districts of this county, which is being supervised by the County Construction Bureau, is nearing completion. The Houshu River, Sitou River, Xinlu Bridge River, and Cai亭 Bridge Port have already been completed and inspected by the Construction Bureau. The Panshu Port in the Seventh District and the Xin'an Creek in the Third District have also been completed. Zhang, the bureau chief, sent technicians Xu and Huang to the countryside yesterday to inspect and accept them. The river channels in Banqiao Port and Beiqifang浜 have not yet been completed, and a telegram has been sent to urge them to speed up the work to facilitate farmland irrigation.

Spring Cocoons Will Soon Appear on the Market 115

In the spring silkworm season in Jiangsu Province this year, various farms produced a total of 1,595,244 clean silkworm cards. After exporting 400,000 cards to Zhejiang Province, more than 1,190,000 cards are left for use in this province. In addition, there are 50,000 Japanese cards. Assuming that each silkworm card yields about 30 catties of silkworm cocoons, the spring silkworms in this province can produce about 400,000 piculs. According to the regulations of the Economic Commission, which convert the price at 30 yuan per picul of fresh cocoons, the total amount of cocoon money flowing into the rural areas of the province will reach 12 million yuan. In this county, the number of spring cards released to silkworm farmers by the model district is 174,209, the number sold at retail by various farms is 65,755, and the number ordered by card vendors is 159,037. The total number of cards in Wuxi is 399,0516, which can produce more than 120,000 piculs of fresh cocoons. Currently, silkworm farming in the four rural areas is affected by the cold weather, and the timing varies. The early batches have mostly gone up the frames, the middle batches are shedding their skins and opening their leaves, and the late batches are still in their third instar. The market price of mulberry leaves is 1.5 to 2 yuan per picul for branches and stems, and 3 to 3.5 yuan per picul for leaves. In addition, the registration of cocoon shops and leaf shops has been completed. The date for collecting cocoons is expected to begin on the 3rd or 4th of next month. The cocoon price is expected to be 30 yuan per picul for improved varieties and 20 yuan per picul for native varieties.

The dispute over the transfer of Chongming and Shengsi Islands has been referred to the Ministry of Interior, which has consulted with Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to schedule a joint survey. Ge Tan, the Commissioner of the Nantong District, has agreed with Zhao Cisheng, the Commissioner of Zhejiang Province, to conduct the survey on June 20, and then add their opinions for the Ministry to review and decide.

Jiaxing Strictly Prohibits Underpriced Cocoon Purchases 117

Cocoon shops throughout Jiaxing County have uniformly started weighing native cocoons. Shops buying improved varieties will also start weighing in the following days. The Seventh District Unified Management Office for Cocoon Collection believes that the land price of native cocoons is 11 yuan, and the lowest must be more than 19 yuan. Fearing that various shops will undervalue purchases, which would be detrimental to the interests of silkworm farmers and damage the government's credibility, it has ordered all cocoon shops to comply. If any underprice below the specified price, the fee payment certificate and shipping certificate will be withheld first, and then more severe penalties will be imposed. In addition, an inspection office has been established in Weixin Street, Jiaxing, and inspectors such as Xu Youdan have been assigned to inspect the silk cocoon transport to facilitate tax collection.

After the meeting, there will be a parade throughout the city. Participants must hold small flags with propaganda slogans written on them, and each school will organize a propaganda team to propagate on the main streets.

Hangzhou's Spring Cocoons Have a Bountiful Harvest 121

This year's spring silkworms in Zhejiang Province have been developing well due to the recent warm weather. The weighing of native cocoons has already begun and will be completely finished around the end of the month. The overall harvest is about 70% of a normal year. The weighing of improved varieties will begin in the following days. The cocoon price is around 32 yuan. The government has strictly cracked down on merchants lowering prices, resulting in prices exceeding the standard price. The harvest is expected to be completely finished around mid-June. The harvest in Jiaxing, Shaoxing, Xiaoshan, Anji, and Xiaofeng counties is slightly worse, about 70-80%, while the remaining 20 counties have a full harvest, with an overall harvest of about 90%.

Aftermath of Gunfight Between Bandits and Police in Ningbo 122

Since the gunfight between bandits and police in Andong Town, Yuyao some days ago, in which one bandit was killed, detective chief Hu Guichuan and two detectives were injured, rumors have spread that the bandit gang is still planning to gather people to retaliate and has sent a letter threatening the town head, Chen Shun-jun, not to report the matter to the authorities or request reinforcements. Zhang Jintang, the chief of the Third District of the tax police stationed in the town, also received a threatening letter from bandits, asking him not to send troops to assist Hu Guichuan. As a result, the situation is tense, the local area is extremely chaotic, and people are particularly uneasy. Everyone fled the area at night. It is reported that there are more than 60 bandits involved in this plot, all former subordinates of the Communist Party member Fei Dezhao, who had already been executed. In order to stabilize the public's morale and investigate and arrest a large number of criminals, a request has been made to the county government to send troops to suppress the bandits, and a large number of teams have been gathered for defense.

Careless Silkworm Roasting Kills Four in Xiaoshan 123

The Jin family, a farming family in Shushan Village, Dongxiang, Xiaoshan, recently experienced cold and rainy weather. All the silkworms had mostly gone up the frames and were unwilling to spin silkworm thread. On the 27th, they used fire to roast them near the silkworm mountain to warm them. Unexpectedly, after 12:00 midnight, the whole family fell asleep, and the sparks spread to the grass on the silkworm mountain. Suddenly, red light rose everywhere, and the smoke filled the house. By the time the family realized it, the fire was raging and could not be controlled. Also, because the ladder had been burned, all four members of the family, both male and female, could not escape and were all buried in the fire. It was truly tragic.

Customs Announces Smuggling in North China Remains Rampant 125

Tax Revenue Loss This Month Does Not Decrease Compared to Last Month

Amounting to a Huge Six Million Yuan in Twenty Days

Central News Agency: Regarding the smuggling incidents in North China, the Customs authorities had previously issued a detailed report, published by the Central News Agency until the end of April this year. Now there is a second report, briefly describing the smuggling situation in North China in the first and middle ten days of May, which is disclosed as follows:

During the three weeks from May 1st to May 20th, the smuggling situation showed an increasing trend. Not only did the total amount of smuggled goods increase, but also the types of smuggled goods emerged in an endless stream. From the war zone west to the Beining Road area, wherever trains can pass, smuggled goods are rampant and unimpeded. The revenue of the Tianjin Customs is decreasing daily. Its tax revenue depends only on a few goods with extremely low tax rates and bulky items that are not easily transported by rail, such as machinery and hardware. It is estimated that the tax revenue loss in the three weeks reached a total of 6 million yuan, an average of 2 million yuan per week, which is about the same as the amount in April. The goods that are smuggled the most are white sugar, rayon, and cigarette paper. In addition, there are kerosene, lubricating oil, piece goods, pigments, iron wire, bicycle parts, seeds, apples, medicines, butter, toothpaste, tires, canned food, food, fruit juice, cosmetics, raincoats, soda, candles, nails, mica flakes, hardwood, kerosene, needles, beans, milk, cotton, silk braids, rubber shoes, batteries, and so on, in all shapes and sizes, without exception. The most noteworthy is the increase in kerosene and liquor. It is particularly hoped that the liquor is not needed for the manufacture of heroin. In addition, there were two cases of military fire, which are also very noteworthy. Now, the statistics of smuggled goods arriving at Tianjin East Railway Station in the three weeks up to May 17 are as follows:

Based on the above estimates, the tax revenue loss in the three weeks reached a total of 6 million yuan, an average of 2 million yuan per week. The import locations of smuggled goods are mostly in Nanlizhuang, Nandasi, and Beidaihe, which are not trading ports permitted by treaty. The Chinese government has the right to confiscate these cargo ships and their goods. However, the Japanese authorities do not allow Chinese customs anti-smuggling vessels to perform their duties there, so China is absolutely unable to protect its treaty rights. Although the Customs authorities are often subject to violent interference, they are still doing their best to maintain their dignity within the possible scope. On May 16, the customs patrol team seized seven cars of smuggled goods transported from Qinhuangdao in the Mengjiadian area, full of beer and Japanese wine. Although the area is within the territory of the Hebei-East puppet organization, the patrol team finally detained it. Afterwards, two Japanese came and claimed that the goods had been taxed in Hebei-East, and demanded their release. Otherwise, the Hebei-East authorities would not recognize the tax payment certificate of the Customs authorities. They were aggressive and unreasonable. The matter is still under negotiation and has not been resolved. However, the Japanese consulate seems unwilling to support the Japanese, as they are deeply afraid that these smuggled goods will leak into the puppet Manchukuo and cause disturbances. The Hebei-East puppet organization has set up a patrol office in Beitang on the 18th, which is headed by two Japanese. This matter is quite noteworthy, because Beitang is outside the war zone and not in the Hebei-East puppet organization area.

Seamen's and Grocery Industry Association Encourages Industry Colleagues to Report Smuggled Goods 126

Regulations and Procedures Compiled into a Booklet

Do Your Best to Assist with Strict Attention

The Shanghai Maritime Products and Grocery Industry Association, in view of the expanding smuggling in North China, issued a notice to all industry colleagues, saying: Since the scope of smuggling in North China has been expanding day by day, the sales of national goods are on the verge of extinction, and the industry and commerce in various places are also greatly affected. According to the Customs estimates, the tax loss in the recent two or three months has reached as much as 30 million yuan. As a result, it not only affects the income of the national treasury, but also affects the credit of foreign debts guaranteed by tariffs. Not only that, due to the exclusion of smuggled goods, legitimate commodities cannot be sold. As a result, factories stop work and workers lose their jobs. How important is its relationship to the national economy and the people's livelihood? Thinking of this, we cannot help but shudder. In view of the seriousness of the smuggling incidents, the government has successively promulgated various anti-smuggling laws and regulations in order to remedy the situation. At this point, we can only embrace the determination to save ourselves and save the country, and learn from each other to assist the government in the implementation of anti-smuggling measures in order to alleviate the current difficulties. Although these smuggled goods have not yet invaded Shanghai, in view of the reports of smuggled goods flooding North China and the price being no guarantee, it is difficult to guarantee that some people who see profit and forget righteousness will not try to transport and dump them in Shanghai. If so, if we do not pay attention, we are always in danger of being deceived and falling into the net of the law. It is the duty of this association to compile the recently promulgated "Provisional Regulations for Punishing Tax Evasion" and "Provisional Regulations for Inspecting the Transportation and Sales of Imported Goods" into a booklet and distribute them to all industry colleagues for reference. If any smuggled goods are found, it is especially important to report them to the association for handling. This is the power granted to the association by the government, and we, as members of the industry, should do our best to assist and pay close attention to it. Please do not neglect it. This is our sincere hope. We hereby notify you, for your public information.

Jiangsu Province Ordered All Counties to Strictly Prohibit Copper Coins from Leaving the Country Yesterday 129

Those with Ministry of Finance Passports Are Not Subject to This Restriction

The Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday issued an order to the county governments of Shanghai Baoshan and other counties, saying: "Since the central government implemented legal tender, the exchange rates of copper coins in various counties have been uneven. Traders from counties with low copper coin prices buy copper coins and purchase goods from counties with high copper coin prices in an attempt to make profits. The impact has resulted in some counties having an excess of copper coins while others lack them. Although the central government has ordered the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to accept and exchange them, the counties without the three banks are still inevitably subject to the above-mentioned abuses. In order to remedy the market, the export of large amounts of copper coins is prohibited. If they are to be carried to the locations of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications for exchange, the proof documents must be checked before being released. This method will maintain the balance of the number of copper coins in each county and will not hinder the central government's promotion of legal tender. However, the Central Bank, Bank of China, or other firms that have transportation of copper coins with passports from the Ministry of Finance due to the relationship of the regulator should still not be restricted by the preceding provisions, with a view to giving equal consideration." After the Ministry of Finance telegraphed the above provisions to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Jiangsu Provincial Government ordered all counties to comply.

Implementation of the Sino-American Monetary Agreement: Foreign Exchange Increasingly Stabilized 132

Part of the Silver Will Be Shipped to the United States for Deposit

Overdrafts Can Be Obtained When Necessary to Consolidate Foreign Exchange

After the Central, China, and Communications Banks received orders from the Ministry of Finance to buy and sell foreign exchange without restrictions, foreign exchange transactions have been concentrated in these three banks, and prices have been very stable. Since the establishment of the Sino-American Monetary Agreement, our country has complied with the agreement and shipped part of its silver to the United States for deposit. Overdrafts can be obtained when necessary, with the aim of stabilizing foreign exchange. Therefore, foreign exchange stability is becoming increasingly consolidated. For example, the foreign exchange rates announced by the Central Bank yesterday were: London at one shilling and two and a half pence, New York at twenty US dollars, Paris at 458 francs, Berlin at 75 marks, Japan at 103 yen, and Hong Kong at 93 Hong Kong dollars, the same as in recent days. There has been no significant fluctuation since the reform of the monetary system on November 4th of last year.

New Cocoons Continuously Arrive in Shanghai: Silk Factories Prepare to Start Work 133

This Year's Fresh Cocoons from Jiangsu and Zhejiang Total One Million Dan

The Loan Syndicate Continues to Accept Applications for Cocoon Purchase Loans

Xin Xin News Agency reports: This year, the spring cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, after the National Economic Council and the Sericulture Improvement Committee dispatched male and female instructors to various regions to provide guidance, have developed well and hatched properly. The output, although not as high as expected due to the cold weather, is still significantly better than last year. It is estimated that Jiangsu Province has about 600,000 dan of improved and native breeds combined, Zhejiang Province has about 310,000 dan of improved breeds and about 180,000 dan of native breeds. The total fresh cocoons from the two provinces amount to one million dan.

Syndicate Continues to Provide Loans

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Spring Cocoon Purchase Loan Syndicate, formed by various banks in the city, after processing loan applications for cocoon purchases on the 6th of this month, has already closed the application period for silk cocoon merchants in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces on the 20th and 25th of this month, respectively, having loaned out a total of more than 6 million yuan. Cocoon merchants in various parts of Zhejiang Province have already started purchasing cocoons at the standard prices set by the Zhejiang Sericulture Control Association. Due to the weather impact in Jiangsu Province, the cocoon season is later, and cocoon merchants in various places will have to delay cocoon purchases until the 4th or 5th of next month. In order to facilitate loan acquisitions by silk factories and other cocoon merchants, the loan syndicate has made special arrangements to continue accepting applications, scheduled to close on the 2nd of next month. At the same time, after the Zhejiang Cocoon and Silk Control Association borrowed 5 million yuan from the bank, it has also dispatched personnel to various regions to start purchasing cocoons.

Silk Factories Prepare to Start Work

Silk factories in Shanghai, Wuxi, Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and other places, because this year the banks organized a loan syndicate to purchase cocoons, and the loan procedures are more convenient than in previous years, have mostly borrowed from the syndicate to purchase cocoons. Now that the spring cocoons will soon be purchased in succession, they have all started preparing to arrange the start of work. The Cocoon and Silk Association has also purchased 1,000 new-style silk reeling machines and distributed them to various silk factories for application as an improvement model. The 36 silk factories in Shanghai, including China, Guangyuan, Xiancheng, Changji, Xingchang Tongyu, Yihe, Jiuyu, Huasheng, and Xinchang, are particularly busy repairing machinery and renovating factory buildings, and will start work after the new cocoons arrive in Shanghai.

New Cocoons Shipped to Shanghai for Storage

This year, silk factories and other cocoon merchants that purchase spring cocoons mostly borrow from the loan syndicate to purchase them. Therefore, when purchasing cocoons, they uniformly purchase them at the announced standard cocoon price, report the amount of cocoons purchased each day to the supervisor sent by the syndicate for review, and bake them into dry cocoons. After being packed into packages, they are immediately transported to the warehouse designated by the syndicate or the factory warehouse for storage. Therefore, the new cocoons shipped from Shaoxing, Haining, Chongde, and other places to Shanghai via the Shanghai-Nanjing, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Shanghai-Ningbo railways have been stored separately in bank warehouses. It is reported that a large batch will continue to arrive within a few days.

Improved Black Tea Directly Exported: First Opening Yesterday 134

A Total of 2,000 Boxes Were Transacted

Highest Price Was 260 Yuan

Shenshi News Agency reports: The Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee will implement direct foreign trade of black tea this year. All black tea transported from Qimen in Anhui Province and Ningzhou in Jiangxi Province will be stored in designated warehouses by the Transportation and Sales Department. Decorations, etc. will be sorted out to suit the sales channels of foreign merchants. Recently, more than 13,000 boxes of new tea have arrived in Shanghai in succession. The Transportation and Sales Department organized a quality evaluation committee, and selected experienced personnel as committee members to evaluate the quality of the new goods that were transported, and various procedures have been completed. The black tea with the evaluated quality was divided into 105 numbers, and the set price was marked and sent to foreign tea firms the previous week. The opening was originally scheduled for the 25th, but it was postponed again because the foreign merchants requested a bank guarantee. The Transportation and Sales Department replied that the Bank of Communications would provide a guarantee. If the goods delivered within 100,000 yuan and within eight months do not match the tea sample, the guarantor will compensate or return the goods. An agreement has been reached. The foreign firms held a tasting session the day before yesterday, and officially held the opening at 9:00 AM yesterday. Wang Yusan, deputy director of the sales group of the Transportation and Sales Department, presided over the auction. Yesterday, a total of 2,000 boxes of black tea were transacted, divided into 15 numbers. The highest price was 260 yuan, and the lowest price was 100 yuan. On average, the price was higher than last year. The buyers were more than a dozen tea merchants from various countries, including Jardine Matheson, Jinlong, Tongfu, Tianyu, Tianxiang, and Dodwell. It is also known that the black tea transacted yesterday will be packed and exported to meet the needs of the tea market in various countries. As for the payment, it will be delivered one week after loading, according to the usual practice.

The letter and telegram are recorded below: Telegram to Wu Minister of the Ministry of Industry, Nanjing Ministry of Industry Wu Minister Junjian, previously received your face-to-face instructions, urging fellow villagers to open their fish markets. After repeated pleadings, all markets also deeply understood the great difficulties of the department and appreciated the Minister's intentions. They are now being urged to open the market immediately and discuss ways to join the market. If there are real difficulties, I hope the Minister will preside. This telegram is hereby submitted, respectfully requesting your review. Also, the letter to the Yong Fresh Fish Trade Association reads: Dear Sirs, this time, the fish merchants of your association stopped sales due to the fish market, which is deeply regrettable. The Association, based on hometown friendship, has repeatedly stated the difficulties of the fish merchants to Minister Wu in all sincerity. We were instructed to urge all markets to open the market first. All the details have been fully informed to the representatives of each market. We hereby earnestly request your association to urge fellow merchants to understand the Minister's good intentions and open the market immediately, and discuss other ways to join the market. If there are difficulties, the members of our association will be responsible for negotiating with the market authorities and the Ministry of Industry in order to achieve a satisfactory solution. This letter is hereby sent, hoping you will investigate and reply.

Zhongyu Iron Factory: Success with Wood-Burning Engine 137

The Zhongxing Iron Factory at 79 Chengou Jia Road has been selling charcoal engines to various places in Zhejiang and Shaoxing since inventing them the year before last, and they have been quite popular. The factory has recently used firewood to manufacture engines, and the experiment has been successful. Its horsepower ranges from three to twelve horsepower, and the firewood consumption is less than fifty catties a day. Compared with diesel, the price difference is vast. At a time when the countryside is poor and oil prices are soaring, the invention of this engine is of great benefit to the countryside. It is said that the general manager of the factory, Chen Bingxun, has manufactured it in large quantities for society to use for irrigation, rice milling, and oil pressing.

The Inland Waterways Shipping Bureau of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: Ordered to Cease Operations and Close Down 138

All Ships, etc., Will Be Sold Separately

And a Shareholders' Meeting Will Be Held on a Scheduled Date to Decide

Xin Sheng News Agency reports: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Inland Waterways Shipping Bureau, which is owned by the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, after being taken back for self-management, although it has tried its best to rectify the situation, is still burdened by excessive debts. It owes the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company more than 500,000 yuan. Moreover, the development of road transport in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has made transportation more convenient, resulting in operational difficulties. Lao Mian, who is also the manager, submitted a report on the rectification to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. It was ordered to cease operations and close down, and all ships will be sold separately. The order was received last month. The manager and Cai Zengji, general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, agreed to convene a shareholders' meeting on June 25 to decide everything. At the same time, shareholder registration will be processed first. It is found that the bureau has a total of 20 ships, including Hengsheng, Hengji, Hengren, Liyuan, and Hengheng, and 20 cargo ships and tugboats. The routes are Shanghai-Huzhou, Shanghai-Suzhou, Shanghai-Lishui, Shanghai-Xia, Shanghai-Wuxi, Shanghai-Qing, Xia-Hai, and Xi-Li.

Both Ships Run Aground 139

Fulong in Haizhou... Huaqiang in Yuxikou

The Fulong vessel of the Sanbei Company in this port, with a deadweight of 1,911 tons, a length of 263 feet and 2 inches, a width of 38 feet and 3 inches, a depth of 15 feet and 5 inches, a draught of 14 feet, and a speed of 10 nautical miles per hour, was dispatched to Haizhou to transport salt. The vessel was fully loaded with salt on the afternoon of the 18th of this month and set sail. The Fulong vessel suddenly ran aground at Chenjiagang. The reason was that the water level at Chenjiagang had dropped sharply, and the Fulong was heavily loaded with a deep draught, causing the vessel to sink into the shallows. After the accident, the captain repeatedly reversed the engine, trying to get away on its own, but the bottom of the Fulong had sunk deep into the shallows and could not move. Fortunately, the company's Fengpu vessel was also in Haizhou. Upon receiving this news, it immediately sailed to assist. However, the water at the grounding site was too shallow, and the Fengpu vessel could not tow it, and could only look at the sea and sigh helplessly. In despair, the Fulong captain telegraphed Shanghai for help. Upon receiving the news, the Shanghai company immediately sent a telegram ordering the Fulong captain that if it could not get out of the shallows at high tide (these days are during neap tides), then part of the salt in the vessel should be unloaded using barges to reduce the vessel's weight and then try to rescue it. After this telegram was sent, the company received a reply from the vessel captain yesterday saying that the salt merchants were unwilling to bear the losses of dispatching barges to unload the goods and the barge fees, and the bureau had to acknowledge them. As a result, this matter cannot be resolved for the time being. Now we can only sit and wait for the spring tide and then try to tow it out of the shallows.

The Huasheng Company's Huaqiang vessel, managed by Yitaixing in this port, with a deadweight of 5,000 tons, is currently loading coal in the Yangtze River. Yesterday morning, the Huaqiang vessel was fully loaded with coal at Yuxikou, opposite Wuhu, and set sail. Due to the low tide (there is also tidal water rising and falling in Wuhu), it also ran aground. The vessel was fully loaded with coal, the draft was heavy, and it could not move at all. Repeated attempts to escape the shallows failed. Yesterday afternoon, the vessel captain had telegraphed Shanghai to report. Upon receiving the news, Huasheng Company, in addition to informing Tang Jun Danhua of the China Ship Insurance Federation, is discussing the progress of sending a vessel to tow it.

Leather Goods Trade Association: Sends Letter to Chamber of Commerce Suggesting Amendment of Law 141

Stipulating Compulsory Membership of the Trade

The Municipal Leather Goods Manufacturing, Steel Bar Scrap Iron, Paint Woodware, Cattle and Sheep, Machine Noodles, Fish Wheel Kitchen Rice Manufacturing, Green Oil Flower Shell, Pedicab Manufacturing, Flower Tree, Cotton Carding, Dough, Bamboo, and other trade associations jointly sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday suggesting compulsory membership of the trade association. The original text reads: Dear Sirs, Recently, I read a news report (May 29) about Ma Yinchu talking about effective ways to deal with smuggling. Regarding the organization of industrial and commercial trade associations, there is a plan to force the industry to join the association, and the affiliated association is very happy to read it. The organization of the trade association is to promote the interests of the trade and correct the abuses of business in order to promote industrial and commercial development and increase production. However, in recent years, although there are hundreds of trade associations, there is no provision for compulsory membership, and each still goes its own way. For example, competition in the same industry is aimed at imitation and counterfeiting, and reducing materials and lowering prices is the ability. The environment is getting worse and worse, the products are becoming more and more crude, the public loses faith, and the industry has concerns about losing money. If this continues, industry and commerce will collapse. If it can be stipulated by law and compulsory membership is required, and the articles of association are followed, the market price is delineated, and the color of the product is stipulated, there will be no abuses of stealing work and reducing materials, and there will be no worries about price drops and losses. The products will become more and more refined, and the credit will become more and more famous. Foreign goods will be cut off, and industry and commerce will have no hope of development. Today, Mr. Ma Yinchu can care about industry and commerce, which is really admirable. All our industrial and commercial groups should unanimously support and promote its realization. In addition to forwarding it to the Legislative Yuan's Ministry of Industry, we especially recommend that you discuss and forward it to the Legislative Yuan's Ministry of Industry to amend the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Trade Association Law in order to save the collapse of industry and commerce. This is the greatest prayer.

Shanghai Merchant Steam Navigation Bureau Stevedoring Office Strives for Pilotage Rights 154

Telegram from the Shanghai Merchant Steam Navigation Bureau Stevedoring Office: To all newspapers, please note: The China Yangtze River Leading Pilots' Association recently sent a telegram stating that foreign customs officers are manipulating China's pilotage rights, denying the qualifications of personnel trained by the pilotage training center, raising pilotage fees, and restricting the number of pilots, causing China's pilotage industry to be permanently ruined. If we do not urgently seek to save it, the dangerous situation is unimaginable. In addition to having submitted a petition to the Central Executive Committee to promptly abolish the Pilotage Management Committee and transfer it to the direct management of the Ministry of Transportation, it is also stipulated that all pilotage personnel in the country who have been trained and qualified by the Naval Pilotage Training Center and hold certificates, or who have served for more than five years without fault, and have proof from the shipowner, may be exempted from examinations to perform their duties, so as to ensure protection and prevent manipulation by foreigners, taking into account national defense. We also ask all national seamen's organizations to unanimously advocate, assist in appealing, and work together to achieve the goal. Accordingly, domestic pilotage is the guidance of waterways. If it is allowed to be manipulated by foreigners, national defense will be endangered in the event of military action, as evidenced by the past French warships entering the Min River port and Japanese warships entering the Liu River. Moreover, when our country is making every effort to revive the nation, we must not abandon the country's only claim. Remembering the past and tracing the present, we cannot help but feel chills. Our office is willing to lead all members and pledge to be the backing force, and will not stop until the goal of preventing foreigners from manipulating pilotage rights and consolidating national defense is achieved. We hereby send this telegram for your information. Shanghai Merchant Steam Navigation Bureau Stevedoring Office.

Another Way to Inspect Factories: Shanghai Municipal Council Restricts Steam Engines 156

The problem of factory inspection in the concessions has not yet been resolved despite repeated negotiations between the municipal government and the Shanghai Municipal Council. It is now heard that the Shanghai Municipal Council has discussed and decided on the regulations for the installation of steam engines and other pressure machines. According to these regulations, the Shanghai Municipal Council has the right to inspect factories with steam engines and pressure machines in the concessions. New factories that need to install such steam engines and pressure machines in the concessions must also be handled by engineers approved by the Shanghai Municipal Council. The Shanghai Municipal Council has established a review committee for these approved engineers, with five members: three from the International Chamber of Commerce, one from the Chinese Chamber of Commerce, one from the Japanese Chamber of Commerce, and one from the Employers' Federation. Among the six people, only the representative from the Chinese Chamber of Commerce is Chinese. It is now heard that this kind of organization is suspected of infringing on the Chinese government's sovereignty to inspect factories, and the authorities are considering it closely.
